## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: constitutive modeling in materials science (solid mechanics, metal plasticity)
**Analysis**: The task relates stress (sigma) to strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), which is typical for flow stress models in hot or cold forming of metals. Stress usually increases with strain due to work hardening and decreases with temperature due to thermal softening, commonly combined multiplicatively.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (very small strains, below yield point)
- Hollomon power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (large plastic strains, uniform elongation region)
- Swift equation: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (power‑law with initial strain offset)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (power‑law hardening with yield strength)
- Voce saturation model: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturation of flow stress with strain)
- Exponential hardening: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * epsilon) (some FCC metals at high strain)
- Linear thermal softening of modulus: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) (temperature dependent elastic modulus)
- Power‑law hardening with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (temperature‑dependent flow stress, softening with T if c2 negative)
- Thermoplastic additive form: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 + c2 * T**c3 (separate contributions of strain and temperature)
- Johnson‑Cook thermal term: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - (c2 * T)**c3) (thermal softening through homologous temperature power law)
- Kocks‑Mecking type: sigma = c0 + c1 * sqrt(epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (parabolic hardening with temperature factor)
- Arrhenius‑type coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (creep or hot deformation, Zener‑Hollomon related)
- Multiplicative softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 / (1 + c2 * T) (saturation‑like temperature weakening)
- Modified Voce with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon))) * exp(c3 * T) (saturated strain hardening with exponential thermal softening)
- Power‑law with thermal threshold: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - Tref))**c2 (if thermal expansion offsets strains)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening typically follows a sublinear power law (exponent between 0 and 1) → epsilon**c with 0<c<1
- Flow stress saturation with increasing strain often takes an exponential form → 1 - exp(-c*epsilon)
- Thermal softening is usually monotonic and can be linear (-c*T), exponential (exp(-c*T)), or a power of homologous temperature (1 - (T/Tm)**c)
- Temperature and strain effects are nearly always multiplicative when active simultaneously → f(epsilon)*g(T)
- For small elastic strains, stress is proportional to strain → sigma = c*epsilon; for larger plastic strains, a power law dominates
- When a yield stress exists before plastic flow, an additive constant appears → sigma = sigma_yield + f(epsilon)
- In hot deformation, an Arrhenius temperature dependence exp(c/T) often appears, reflecting thermally activated dislocation motion
- The Johnson‑Cook model uses a specific thermal softening term (1 - ((T-Tref)/(Tm-Tref))**m); without melting data, a cheaper surrogate is (1 - c*T) or exp(-c*T)
- Strain‑rate independence (only epsilon and T given) suggests static or quasi‑static loading; temperature affects mainly the softening, not the hardening exponent
- Some models replace strain by an effective strain that subtracts thermal expansion → (epsilon - c*T), leading to a shift in the strain axis with temperature
